review","link":"https://the-gadgeteer.com/?p=304264","description":"\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304260\" 100vw, 689px\"></p>\n<p><strong>REVIEW</strong> – Some backpacks have very specific purposes.  The <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2020/05/12/pakt-travel-backpack-review/\">Pakt Travel Backpack</a> is designed to be a suitcase.  This one is designed <a href=\"https://www.enhancegaming.com/index.php?route=product/product&#38;path=675_839&#38;product_id=11489\" target=\"_blank\">to carry board games</a>.  This one is <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2018/05/20/belkin-classic-pro-laptop-backpack-review/\">for carrying a laptop</a>.  An <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/tag/edc/\">everyday carry</a> backpack, however, needs to find a sweet spot somewhere in the middle of these extremes.  It needs to be able to carry your laptop to the office, your books to class, and your clothes on a two-day business trip as well as have plenty of space for all the odds-and-ends that you might want to bring along.  Is the Drifter backpack from Targus the right bag for the job?  Read on to find out!</p>\n<h2>What is it?</h2>\n<p>The name might make you think that this is only a bag for carrying your laptop around, but the <a href=\"https://amzn.to/2YABBWK\" rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\">16″ Drifter II Laptop Backpack</a> is much more than that.  It’s an everyday carry backpack that has a secure compartment for a laptop but also has plenty of storage to help out employees, students, and travelers alike.  Its page on Targus’ website says that it is “built to last and made for travel.”</p>\n<h2>What’s in the box?</h2>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304261\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-2-645x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"645\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-2-645x800.jpg 645w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-2-202x250.jpg 202w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-2.jpg 726w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 645px) 100vw, 645px\"></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Just the backpack</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Hardware specs</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Water-resistant bottom</li>\n<li>Constructed of nylon materials</li>\n<li>Works with up to 16” laptops</li>\n<li>18 liter carrying capacity</li>\n<li>17.00″ x 20.00″ x 5.00″ (W x H x D)</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Design and features</h2>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304262\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-3-800x781.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"781\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-3-800x781.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-3-256x250.jpg 256w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-3-768x750.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-3.jpg 900w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>The design of this backpack is fairly standard.  It has a compartment for the laptop in the back, a large compartment in the middle, two smaller compartments up front, and a host of specialty compartments all around.  The bag is mostly black with a dash of grey on the front, and there are a handful of bright yellow accents, just enough to give it a splash of color.  The bag is reservedly attractive, providing a dignified look that would be appropriate in most offices and classrooms.</p>\n<h3>Installation and setup</h3>\n<p>No installation is required.  Take the backpack out of its bag, remove a label or two, and it’s ready to go.</p>\n<h3>Performance</h3>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304263\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-4-800x708.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"708\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-4-800x708.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-4-282x250.jpg 282w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-4-768x680.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-4.jpg 900w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>First, let’s look at the various compartments in the Drifter, starting with the one in the back for the laptop.  As the name suggests, this backpack can hold up to 16” laptops. When I opened the zipper, I found there were actually 3 spaces in this compartment.  There’s one for the laptop, which easily accommodated my 15” MacBookPro; in fact, I think I could put two more laptops in there with it.  It has extra padding in front and behind as well as below, which I very much like, and a strap with Velcro to make sure the laptop doesn’t slip out.  My laptop should be well protected.  There’s a smaller, zippered mesh space, perfect for cables or a mouse.  The main space in the middle could hold a power brick, a mousepad, or anything else associated with a laptop.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304265\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-5-718x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"718\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-5-718x800.jpg 718w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-5-224x250.jpg 224w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-5-768x855.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-5.jpg 808w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 718px) 100vw, 718px\"></p>\n<p>The next compartment is the main compartment.  It’s in the middle of the bag, and when I put my hand down into it and push towards the front of the bag, it extends out a full 7”, which provides a deceptively large amount of space.  I could easily fit enough clothes for a two-day business trip or a casual weekend at a friend’s house.  I put in eight full-sized, hardcover books, more than I would enjoy carrying around, and still had room left over!  This compartment also has a space to slip in a magazine and another zippered mesh space.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304266\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-6-756x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"756\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-6-756x800.jpg 756w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-6-236x250.jpg 236w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-6-768x812.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-6.jpg 851w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 756px) 100vw, 756px\"></p>\n<p>In front of the main compartment is a smaller one, about the right size for a couple of notebooks.  It’s deep but doesn’t have much volume.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304267\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-7-800x596.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"596\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-7-800x596.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-7-300x223.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-7-768x572.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-7.jpg 900w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>At the very front is a smaller compartment with a host of pockets and spaces for storing all the little things that I inevitably need to take with me.  It can hold <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2020/04/27/mophie-powerstation-with-power-delivery-review/\">a power bank</a>, pens and pencils, USB keys, <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2020/02/15/the-fox-in-the-forest-card-game-review/\">a card game</a>, and so much more.</p>\n<p>Scattered around the Drifter are a host of smaller pockets.  On the front is a 4” padded and zippered pocket, perfect for slipping in your phone or a small journal.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304268\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-8-800x539.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"539\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-8-800x539.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-8-300x202.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-8-768x517.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-8.jpg 900w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>On the top, just behind the handle, is a zipped compartment that is lined with soft fabric.  This is the perfect place to put my phone, <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2019/12/24/godbole-classic-and-slim-bifold-wallets-review/\">Godbolé wallet</a>, ring, watch, and other personal items when I’m going through security at the airport.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304269\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-9-800x508.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"508\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-9-800x508.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-9-300x191.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-9-768x488.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-9.jpg 900w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>On the back of the backpack, somewhat concealed in one of the areas of the padding, is a hidden, 10” pocket.  If I were traveling overseas and doing some sight-seeing in a big city like London or Kuala Lumpur, then I would definitely use this to hide my most important valuables, like travelers checks, my passport, some extra cash, or a slip of paper with emergency phone numbers.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304270\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-10-798x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"798\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-10-798x800.jpg 798w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-10-249x250.jpg 249w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-10-250x250.jpg 250w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-10-768x770.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-10.jpg 898w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 798px) 100vw, 798px\"></p>\n<p>Each side of the backpack has a pair of spaces.  One is for a smaller-size water bottle, held in place with some stretchy material, and another is a long, thin zippered pocket that looks like a great place to put some snacks.</p>\n<p>When all of these are considered together, it’s obvious that the Drifter has a lot of storage capacity and a wide variety of pockets and compartments for a wide variety of items.  I think it has a place for everything I would want to bring on a trip.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304271\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-11-762x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"762\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-11-762x800.jpg 762w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-11-238x250.jpg 238w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-11-768x807.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-11.jpg 857w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 762px) 100vw, 762px\"></p>\n<p>Second, let’s consider the comfort of the backpack as a whole.  There are four areas of thick padding on the back, and the lower one is designed to provide lumbar support.  The straps are also padded along the entire inside length.  Taken together, they make wearing the Drifter pleasantly comfortable.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304272\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-12-800x431.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"431\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-12-800x431.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-12-300x162.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-12-768x414.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-12.jpg 900w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>The straps can be adjusted in front, which tightens or loosens the backpack.  The only thing missing is a second set of adjustments on top of the straps, like those on <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2019/08/01/osprey-tropos-everyday-backpack-review/\">the Osprey Tropos</a>, which help to raise or lower the position of the backpack on the back.  This would be a nice addition but isn’t necessary.</p>\n<h3>Extra Features</h3>\n<p>The Drifter is made of durable nylon material, and thus I expect it will hold up under and normal wear and tear for many years.  The nylon is water-resistant, as is the specially-designed base, but it’s not waterproof, and Targus doesn’t advertise any rain covers that can be purchased.  I think this backpack will be fine in a brief shower, but I wouldn’t want to trust my laptop to it during a downpour or while hiking all day in the rain.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304273\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-13-800x486.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"486\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-13-800x486.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-13-300x182.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-13-768x467.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/targus-drifter-13.jpg 900w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>The handle is made of sturdy plastic, and I can see the thick, metal wire that runs through it and the metal grommets that support it on each side.  The zippers are also sturdy, and I didn’t experience any problems opening or closing them.  I believe that this is a backpack that will last a long time; it’s an investment worth making.</p>\n<h2>What I like</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Spacious carrying capacity</li>\n<li>Many, varied storage compartments and pockets</li>\n<li>Strong, durable construction</li>\n<li>Comfortable padding</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>What I’d change</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Nothing</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Final thoughts</h2>\n<p>I’m very pleased with Targus’ 16” Drifter Laptop backpack.  I love all the various places to store items, the padding on the laptop pocket, the huge storage space in the central compartment, and the secret pocket in the back padding.  It has so many different places to store items that I don’t think I will ever say to myself, “I can’t find a place to put this!”  The construction is solid, and I believe that the Drifter will last a long time.  If you’re in the market for an everyday backpack, particularly one that can carry a laptop, then without any reservations I recommend that you put this backpack on your shortlist.</p>\n<p><strong>Price</strong>: $47.74 on Amazon, $84.99 on Targus’ online 13:50:41","updatedTime":"2020-08-31 13:50:41","title":"Ecovacs auto-emptying charging base review – Make the OZMO T8 vacs even better","link":"https://the-gadgeteer.com/?p=304463","description":"\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304467\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-4.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"536\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-4.jpg 536w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-4-168x250.jpg 168w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 536px) 100vw, 536px\"></p>\n<p><strong>REVIEW</strong> – I love my robot vacuum.  Specifically, it is an <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2020/06/07/ecovacs-deebot-ozmo-t8-aivi-robot-vacuum-mop-review/\">Ecovacs Deebot OZMO T8 AIVI</a> that I reviewed in June 2020. What I don’t like is how often I have to empty the teeny, tiny dustbin that all robot vacuums have. If only there was a way to not have to empty that dustbin every time I vacuumed.  If I only had to deal with the dirt and dust once a month, wouldn’t that be great? Ecovacs has heard my cries and has released a new auto-emptying recharging base.  Could this make my dust-free dreams come true or will it just suck?</p>\n<h2>What is it?</h2>\n<p>The Ecovacs auto-empty station is a replacement charging base for Ecovacs T8 series robotic vacuums – the OZMO T8 AIVI and the newly announced OZMO T8. Along with recharging, it will empty the dustbin, capturing all the dirt and debris into a vacuum bag located in the canister.</p>\n<h2>What’s in the box?</h2>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304477\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-14.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"580\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-14.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-14-300x218.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-14-768x557.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Base charging pad</li>\n<li>Carpet ramp for base pad</li>\n<li>Canister with bag installed</li>\n<li>Extra bag</li>\n<li>Replacement dust bin with dust evacuation doors</li>\n<li>Dust bin pleated high-performance filter</li>\n<li>Dust bin sponge filter</li>\n<li>Screwdriver and three screws (in silver pouch) to attach the canister to the base pad</li>\n<li>Key to remove dust bin evacuation covers (in an envelope next to dust bin)</li>\n<li>Power cord</li>\n<li>Setup instruction page</li>\n<li>Quick start guide</li>\n<li>FCC compliance card</li>\n<li>User guide</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Hardware specs</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Dimensions: 17.5″h x 12″w x 17″d</li>\n<li>Bag capacity: 2L (about 30 days of dust and debris)</li>\n<li>Vacuum compatibility: Ecovacs OZMO T8 AIVI and OZMO T8</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Design and features</h2>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304473\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-10.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"467\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-10.jpg 467w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-10-146x250.jpg 146w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 467px) 100vw, 467px\"></p>\n<p>The auto-empty station, or “base” to make this review much easier to read, replaces the included charging base that comes with the robot vacuum.  It has a modified charging base that includes charging contacts (the silver pads in the black rectangle) and vacuum openings (the two large holes near the front of the base).  Those two holes allow the base to 1) blow high-velocity air into the dustbin, and, 2) suck that air and dirt into a bag.</p>\n<p>The bag is mounted inside the press-to-open canister on the back of the base. At the front of the lid, on the canister, there is an indicator LED that lights during charging and emptying operations.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304472\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-9.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"574\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-9.jpg 574w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-9-179x250.jpg 179w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 574px) 100vw, 574px\"></p>\n<p>If you have ever installed a bag in a vacuum, you’ll do fine here.  Each bag has a cardboard mount that slips into a channel in the back of the canister.  The bag will hold about two liters of dust and debris.  It is thoughtfully designed with a cover that automatically deploys when you pull the blue tab to remove the bag, trapping all that nastiness in the bag.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304471\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-8.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"627\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-8.jpg 627w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-8-196x250.jpg 196w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 627px) 100vw, 627px\"></p>\n<p>The entire base and canister is made from pebble-finished gray plastic and feels very solid.  The carpet ramp shown in an earlier photo is used if you set up the base on a carpeted floor.  Since I have the base on a hard floor, I did not use it.</p>\n<p>On the back of the base, we find the power port and a cord tender integrated into the base and canister. My power socket is close to where I have the base, so it would be nice if the cord tender held more core.  A minor quibble.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304468\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-5.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"707\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-5.jpg 707w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-5-221x250.jpg 221w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 707px) 100vw, 707px\"></p>\n<p>The base also comes with a newly designed dustbin.  On the new dustbin on the left, you can see the input and output doors on the left and right.  These springloaded doors open automatically during dustbin cleaning.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304476\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-13.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"230\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-13.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-13-300x86.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-13-768x221.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<h3>Setup</h3>\n<p>Setting up the base comes with a few steps. First, open up that silver foil envelope. Inside, we find a screwdriver and three screws.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304475\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-12.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"630\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-12.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-12-300x236.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-12-768x605.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>These are used to attach the base module to the canister.  You slide the canister onto the base and then you screw them together from the bottom.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304474\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-11.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"556\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-11.jpg 556w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-11-174x250.jpg 174w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 556px) 100vw, 556px\"></p>\n<p>The next change happens to the robot itself.  To accommodate the cleaning doors in the new dustbin, you have to remove port covers in the dustbin receptacle in the robot.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304470\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-7.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"455\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-7.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-7-300x171.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-7-768x437.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>The two small doors to the left and right of the barcode sticker cover those openings.  You use the included key tool to unlock and remove those covers. I tossed the covers and the removal key into the old dustbin, so I might be able to find them if I ever need them again.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304469\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-6.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"750\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-6.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-6-267x250.jpg 267w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-6-768x720.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>Once the base is assembled and the robot is modified, you’re ready to go.</p>\n<h3>Performance</h3>\n<p>Vacuuming performance isn’t affected at all, as expected. Charging happens just like before.  The only difference is that now, at the end of vacuuming, the base can empty the dustbin so you don’t have to.</p>\n<p>The robot can tell that it now has this base.  The app changes to reflect this.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304543\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-15.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"519\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-15.jpg 519w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-15-162x250.jpg 162w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 519px) 100vw, 519px\"></p>\n<p>If you look just below and to the right of the map, a new “Dust collection” button appears.  This allows you to manually suck the debris out of the dustbin. But doing things manually is just so old school.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304465\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"384\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-2.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-2-300x144.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-2-768x369.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>Of course, the app comes with a setting that allows you to have the robot automatically empty the dustbin when it returns to the base.  When it is emptying, the app pops up a notification, just in case the loud vacuuming sound doesn’t tip you off.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304466\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-3.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"360\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-3.jpg 360w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/exovacs-base-3-113x250.jpg 113w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\"></p>\n<p>How loud is it?  About as loud as a traditional vacuum.</p>\n<div class=\"ast-oembed-container\"><iframe title=\"Ecovacs self-emptying base for The Gadgeteer\" width=\"1200\" height=\"675\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/XPe1d5svX4c?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div>\n<p>As you can hear in the video, the robot plays voice prompts, letting you know exactly what’s going on. A voice prompt and app notification will tell you when the bag is full and needs to be replaced.  Believe me, you don’t want to hear that very often.</p>\n<p>The biggest drawback of the auto-empty station is the cost of the bags.  Excovacs is selling bags for a pricey $19.99 for three bags – that’s about $6.66 per bag.  Assuming that you use one bag every 30 days, you’re on the hook to Ecovacs for about $80 every year.  I get that the bags are hypoallergenic and have that nifty self-sealing feature, but, c’mon.  Kirby has long been a very expensive vacuum to both purchase and maintain. I can find Kirby MicroAllergen HEPA bags for less than five bucks a bag.</p>\n<h2>What I like</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>One month without emptying the dustbin – woo!</li>\n<li>Self-closing vacuum bags – nice!</li>\n<li>Does a great job evacuating the dustbin</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>What I’d change</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>The cord tender could be a little bigger for those of us that have an outlet right next to the base</li>\n<li>Make the price for bags a little more reasonable</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Final thoughts</h2>\n<p>I honestly expected this to do a so-so job.  When I empty the dustbin, the screen is typically pretty clogged with dust, dirt, and my wife’s medium-length hair.  With it all stuck to the filter screen, I just figured much of it would remain.  Wow, was I wrong. The base blows high-velocity air into the dustbin through one of the new dustbin doors.  This loosens all the debris from the filter.  At the same time, it sucks air through the other new dustbin door, pulling all that loosened material into the bag.  I was shocked at how clean the dustbin was after the cleaning cycle.  A robot that not only cleans but cleans up after itself.  Who would have imagined? But, the high cost of bags tarnishes the shine a little bit for me.  Here’s hoping that someone discounts them.</p>\n<p><strong>Price</strong>: $249.99<br>\n<strong>Where to buy</strong>: <a href=\"https://www.ecovacs.com/us/deebot-robotic-vacuum-cleaner/Auto-Empty-Station\" target=\"_blank\">Ecovacs</a><br>\n<strong>Source</strong>: The sample of this product was provided by <a href=\"https://www.ecovacs.com/us\" target=\"_blank\">Ecovacs</a>.</p>\n  <p>Filed in categories: <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/category/reviews/\" rel=\"category tag\">Reviews</a></p><p>Tagged: 201w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 643px) 100vw, 643px\"></p>\n<p><strong>REVIEW</strong> – Over the past few years, my younger son has developed an interest in jazz, both as a musician and as an enthusiast. He has been collecting vinyl records and has been, in his words, “slumming it” with my vintage turntable and a dedicated phonographic amp and Bluetooth transmitter (I keep trying to explain that my vintage turntable was an upper-end consumer model, but it’s old so…).  I also have a number of albums on vinyl that are either unavailable digitally (CD or download) or that I have been loathe to purchase again. The Electrohome Kingston 7-in-1 record player, which also includes a CD player, radio, Bluetooth / USB playback, and recording, looks like a solution to many of our problems.</p>\n<h2>What is it?</h2>\n<p>The Electrohome Kingston 7-in-1 record player (Model RR75) is a retro-styled multi-function device.  The Kingston 7-in-1 features the following functions:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>phonograph</li>\n<li>CD player</li>\n<li>AM / FM radio</li>\n<li>Bluetooth receiver</li>\n<li>USB playback</li>\n<li>auxiliary input</li>\n<li>Recording onto USB thumb drive from phonograph, CD, radio, Bluetooth, or auxiliary input</li>\n</ul>\n<p>In addition to the four integrated speakers, the Kingston sports a headphone jack and stereo RCA outputs.</p>\n<h2>What’s in the box?</h2>\n<p>The Kingston 7-in-1 Record Player comes packed in a relatively plain cardboard box. It is shipped surrounded by expanded polystyrene and is wrapped in a protective plastic envelope with an obligatory desiccant pack.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-304247 aligncenter\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-02.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-02.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-02-188x250.jpg 188w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>The power cord, remote (with batteries–nice to see), and user guide are packed in the bottom of the box in a separate bag. The quick-start guide is placed on the record spindle.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-304248 aligncenter\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-03.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-03.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-03-300x225.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-03-768x576.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-304251\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-06.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"600\" https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-06-768x576.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<h2>Hardware specs</h2>\n<p>The pertinent hardware specifications include (quoting from the Electrohome website):</p>\n<table id=\"product-attribute-specs-table\" class=\"data-table\">\n<tbody>\n<tr class=\"even\">\n<th class=\"label\">inish</th>\n<td kg)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr class=\"even\">\n<th class=\"label\">Amplifier Power</th>\n<td class=\"data last\">35 Watts</td>\n</tr>\n<tr class=\"odd\">\n<th class=\"label\">Auto Stop</th>\n<td class=\"data last\">Yes</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>This particular unit is finished in cherry wood veneer.</p>\n<h2>Design and features</h2>\n<h3>Setup</h3>\n<p>Setting up the Kingston 7-in-1 involved removing various molded pieces of expanded polystyrene, removing the protective film over the front display panel, installing the batteries in the remote, uncapping the stylus (somewhat problematic, see below), lowering the shipping screw (this is the first time I had to lower a screw to unlock a turntable, most of the ones that I have owned, raise a screw to unlock) located next to the tone arm, and plugging in the unit.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-304251 aligncenter\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-06.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-06.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-06-300x225.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-06-768x576.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></p>\n<p>When I followed the directions for uncapping the stylus, I found that the actual needle and it’s carrier arm had folded backward and didn’t allow for proper operation of the phonograph.  It took about 10 minutes of investigation to find the cause and move the needle back into position. There was no apparent damage to the stylus or to my test record and records have played well.</p>\n<h3>Performance</h3>\n<p>My jazz-enthusiast son and I put the Kingston 7-in-1 through its paces during the last few weeks.  His primary interest was being able to play his expanding collection of small-press LPs with headphones so he could riff with the recordings. I was more interested in being able to transcode some of my rare LPs and promotional 45s into MP3s so I could listen to them without worrying about damaging the original vinyl records.</p>\n<p>We are happy to report that the Kingston lived up to its billing. The sound quality from all sources is better than what I was expecting from an all-in-one unit.</p>\n<h4>Auxiliary input</h4>\n<p>Playback from the auxiliary input (1/8″ jack) was more than acceptable. I think part of our problem was that we used an old cable to connect my laptop to the Kingston.  The sound was comparable to the vintage bookshelf speakers that we used for comparison.</p>\n<h4>Bluetooth playback</h4>\n<p>Bluetooth playback was very good.  The sound was clear and at a good volume.</p>\n<h4>CD player</h4>\n<p>The CD player is a main-stream unit without any bells and whistles, just play/pause, stop, skip forward / backward, and eject.</p>\n<h4>Radio</h4>\n<p>We initially had some problems with radio reception, but we re-positioned the built-in antenna and eventually moved the unit away from some potential sources of interference and the problem was solved.  We were able to set and retrieve multiple station presets.</p>\n<h4>Record player</h4>\n<p>The record player function is what my son and I were most interested in.  The Kingston sports a basic turntable without a lot of the automation that those of us of a certain age remember from our younger days. To use the player, you place a record on the turntable, unlock the tone arm, raise the tone arm using the tone arm lever and then manually move the arm over the record and manually lower it. At the end of playback (when the arm reaches the center of the record) the turntable shuts off, but the arm does not automatically return.</p>\n<p>I would have liked to see at least automatic starting / cuing of records and automatic return of the tone arm at the end of playback, but this would add weight, complexity, and cost.  For many these additional features are not worth the risk of failure, additional cost, or weight.</p>\n<h4>USB playback</h4>\n<p>Like most of the other functions of the Kingston, the USB playback quite good (limited of course by the source files). The functions are limited to play/pause, skip forward/back, folder navigation, and special playback: repeat track, repeat folder, repeat all, or shuffle.</p>\n<h4>USB recording</h4>\n<p>The USB recording feature has a few qualifications. The USB drive must be formatted as FAT32 and have a maximum capacity of 32 GB. Files are transcoded as 128 kbps quality. The Kingston supports recording from records, CDs, auxiliary input, or Bluetooth (which is a nice bonus).</p>\n<p>The recording process starts by selecting the source and inserting a compatible USB drive into the USB-A port on the front of the unit. From there the exact process differs depending on the source.</p>\n<p>Recording from a record / aux / Bluetooth, playback is started manually and then the RECORD button on the front of the unit is pressed (I usually reversed these because I split tracks on my computer). Tracks can be manually split during playback by pressing the track skip button on the front panel or on the remote. Recording may also be paused using the play/pause button on either the remote or front panel. Pressing the record button again stops the recording.</p>\n<p>Recording from a CD is more automated. Once the CD is loaded and the USB drive is inserted, pressing record begins the recording process. The skip forward / back buttons are used to cycle through RECORD ONE, RECORD FOLDER, RECORD ALL (I’m not sure what recording a folder on a commercially produced CD means). Again press RECORD to stop recording early.</p>\n<p>The recorded files are stored in sub-directories on the USB drive: /RECORD/EXREC for non-CD sources and /RECORD/COPY for files sourced from CDs.</p>\n<h4>Connecting to an external amplifier</h4>\n<p>The only external amplifier that we had to test this feature with was a dedicated headphone amplifier.  This feature works, but I can’t really comment on the quality of the output because of the test environment.</p>\n<h4>Headphones</h4>\n<p>I found the headphone performance to be a bit of a mixed bag. This may have been due to the headphones that I used and the lack of personalized settings (I’m used to using tuning programs on my computer to compensate for the nuances of my headphones and my age-related hearing loss). My son thought the music sounded fine (we tested using his headphones).</p>\n<h2>What I like</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>All-in-one unit</li>\n<li>Can record from a variety of sources</li>\n<li>Includes a remote (with batteries)</li>\n<li>Easy-to-read, helpful manual</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>What could be improved</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Slightly larger cabinet, so that standard-size LPs don’t stick out the back of the cabinet</li>\n<li>Use of a traditional-style stylus</li>\n<li>Recording from non-CD sources is clumsy — I just recorded whole LPs and then split out the tracks using other software (it reminds me of my days trying to record the top 40 countdown from the radio without also recording the commercials).</li>\n<li>Automatic cuing of LPs and return of the tone arm.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Final thoughts</h2>\n<p>The Electrohome Kingston 7-in-1 Record Player is a very nice unit that can fill most of your small-space entertainment needs.  It is certainly going to find a place in our home for many years. The Kingston comes with an easy-to-read and comprehensive manual that answered every question that came up during evaluation, which is a nice change from most consumer electronics these days.</p>\n<p><strong>Price</strong>: $199.99<br>\n<strong>Where to buy</strong>: <a href=\"http://www.electrohome.com\" target=\"_blank\">Electrohome’s e-commerce site</a>, <a href=\"https://amzn.to/32uptYK\" rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\">Amazon</a><br>\n<strong>Source</strong>: The sample of this product was provided by Electrohome.</p>\n  <p>Filed in categories: <a Sailors","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-01.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn47@2020_3/2020/08/31/05-50-44-553_9dbe4d142ec97b66.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-02.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn24@2020_2/2020/08/31/05-50-50-732_ff9d2078c7578595.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-03.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn84@2020_6/2020/08/31/05-50-50-582_f47720fea1a873b0.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Electrohome-Kingston_7in1-06.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn40@2020_1/2020/08/31/05-50-56-790_a1feb870f1cfc4b8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598853041848},{"createdTime":"2020-08-31 13:50:41","updatedTime":"2020-08-31 13:50:41","title":"Nuheara IQbuds2 Max wireless earphones review – your ears will thank you","link":"https://the-gadgeteer.com/?p=304355","description":"\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_7.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304342\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_7.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"469\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_7.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_7-300x235.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></a></p>\n<p><strong>REVIEW</strong> – In 2017, the <i>Over the Counter Hearing Aid Act </i>was passed providing greater public accessibility and affordability with over-the-counter (OTC) hearing aids. Now, many earphone companies offer DIY hearing tests using your iPhone and an app. The results of these hearing tests allow personalized tuning of earphones, which can make them <i>yours. </i>The Australian company, Nuheara, was one of the first to offer a testing app with their <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2017/12/18/nuheara-iqbuds-intelligent-truly-wireless-earbuds-review/\">IQbuds wireless earphones</a> and then the <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2018/06/22/nuheara-iqbuds-intelligent-truly-wireless-earbuds-with-boost-review/\">IQbuds wireless earphones with BOOST</a>. These earphones were revolutionary when they came out, but time—and competition—marches on. Nuheara has just released the new IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max wireless earphones and they are an improvement in every way.</p>\n<h2><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_10.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304339\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_10.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"506\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_10.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_10-296x250.jpg 296w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></a></h2>\n<h2>What is it?</h2>\n<p>The IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max wireless earphones are the latest in Nuheara’s line of totally wireless earphones (they call them “buds”—is that an Australian thing?) that feature Ear ID, which measures hearing levels and delivers calibrated audio to the user. They now include active noise cancelation (ANC).</p>\n<h2><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_13.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304336\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_13.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"501\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_13.jpg 501w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_13-209x250.jpg 209w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 501px) 100vw, 501px\"></a></h2>\n<h2>Specs</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Bluetooth: 5.0; A2DP, aptX</li>\n<li>Sweatproof and water-resistant</li>\n<li>Battery recharging: 90 min.</li>\n<li>5 hour listening time; Total time: 15 hours with 3 recharges from case</li>\n<li>Speaker: 9.2 mm dynamic</li>\n<li>Hearing augmentation: Noise control, World, Directional</li>\n<li>6 pairs of ear tips; 3 silicone, 3 Comply foam</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_5.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304344\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_5.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"552\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_5.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_5-272x250.jpg 272w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></a></h2>\n<h2>Design and features</h2>\n<p>Since reviewing both the original IQ buds and IQ buds with Boost, I can now compare them to the new IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max. The first noticeable improvement is comfort. The Max earphones are more compact, so the fit feels more ergonomic than earlier IQbuds, which weren’t all that comfortable after using a couple of hours. These are way better. I can wear these all day—or until the battery runs out—with no issues. Having said that, the IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones are not the smallest earphones out there. They are still a bit on the large side, but it’s not surprising considering all the tech they hold.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_15.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304334\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_15.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"460\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_15.jpg 460w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_15-192x250.jpg 192w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 460px) 100vw, 460px\"></a></p>\n<p>The IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones are ergonomic in the way they fit into the ear. Place them into the ear with the ear tip in the 6 o’clock position and twist to “lock” into place. The earphone’s shape holds them in place, so you can go about doing chores or exercising without them falling out. About the only thing you can’t do is swim with them. They are sweatproof and water-resistant with an IP54 rating, but not <em>waterproof</em>.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_12.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304337\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_12.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_12.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_12-300x227.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></a></p>\n<p>The earphone shell is matte black plastic and extremely light in weight. They come with 3 sizes of silicone and 3 sizes of Comply foam ear tips. I had no trouble finding a size that fit even though my ears are fairly finicky about ear tips. Included is a cloth bag for protecting the case from scratches.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_4.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304345\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_4.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"491\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_4.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_4-300x246.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></a></p>\n<p>The IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones snap magnetically into their hard case. This adds a level of security against falling out of the case as well as ensuring a solid connection for charging. The 5-hour listening rating isn’t great but will get you through streaming a movie. Battery life using World On and EarID is rated at 8-hours—and that’s where the IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones shine.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Tap-Touch.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304353\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Tap-Touch.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"277\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Tap-Touch.jpg 277w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Tap-Touch-115x250.jpg 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 277px) 100vw, 277px\"></a></p>\n<p> </p>\n<p>Both IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones feature tap touch. each earphone accepts three kinds of taps: short, double, and long tap. Each tap can be set to either Play/pause, Next track, Previous track, Volume up/down, or None. All these choices can be a bit of a learning curve. I have most of the taps set to None since I rely on my iPhone for most of these functions anyway. If you are more tap-tech savvy, you can utilize every setting available. It’s nice to have that choice.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_EarID.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304354\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_EarID.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"277\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_EarID.jpg 277w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_EarID-115x250.jpg 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 277px) 100vw, 277px\"></a></p>\n<p>Before you first use the IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones, Nuheara provides an Ear ID hearing test via their free downloadable app for iOS and Android. The app will not provide a hearing analysis as detailed as an audiologist would (no app can do that) but based on the test’s outcome, it can tune audio to your specific needs. This can help you pick out and understand voices in a crowded environment, like a restaurant, school, or even at home. This has been my hearing issue: I can hear just fine—it’s <i>understanding</i> what’s being said that I have issues with. The IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones help clarify what my ears hear.</p>\n<p>Taking the app’s hearing test is similar to an audiologist test (again, not as detailed). While sitting in a quiet environment, you tap the screen each time you hear the tones, which become quieter in volume, while also changing frequencies. The test results help determine where your particular weaknesses are. For instance, mine is hearing higher frequencies due to aging—a normal occurrence. The app breaks down hearing issues into six frequency levels. It turns out that my right ear has better hearing than my left.</p>\n<p>A cool thing is that you can also take Nuheara’s hearing ID test <a href=\"https://www.nuheara.com/hearing-check/\" target=\"_blank\">online</a>. This way, you can see if your hearing can be improved before purchasing the IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones first. Nuheara provides explanations about the results.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_World_2.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304352\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_World_2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"277\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_World_2.jpg 277w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_World_2-115x250.jpg 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 277px) 100vw, 277px\"></a></p>\n<p>Within this app, there are a few different settings to further customize and dramatically alter the audio. These settings are grouped in what Nuheara calls World ON or OFF. When World is off, all settings are muted. When World is turned on, the following settings become available.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_ANC.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304349\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_ANC.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"277\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_ANC.jpg 277w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_ANC-115x250.jpg 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 277px) 100vw, 277px\"></a></p>\n<p>The first setting is turning Active Noise Canceling (ANC) on and off—more on this later in the review.<span class=\"Apple-converted-space\"> </span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Sinc.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304351\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Sinc.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"277\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Sinc.jpg 277w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Sinc-115x250.jpg 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 277px) 100vw, 277px\"></a></p>\n<p>Sinc helps separate vocals from background noise. It’s controlled by dialing between ambiance and speech. I always have the dial moved towards speech because it helps lower distracting background noise.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_World.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304333\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_World.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"277\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_World.jpg 277w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_World-115x250.jpg 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 277px) 100vw, 277px\"></a></p>\n<p>World EQ increases and decreases both bass and treble. Decreasing bass makes speech sound sharper and more clear at the expense of sounding natural. Voices take on a metallic, “robotic” quality, but are easier to understand. Decreasing (or filtering) treble allows voices to sound much more natural at the expense of clarity. So you have to dial between the two to get the right balance for your hearing. I’m a fan of less treble because to my ears when the treble is filtered more (allowing more bass), audio sounds harsher.<span class=\"Apple-converted-space\"> </span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Focus.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304350\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Focus.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"277\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Focus.jpg 277w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_App_Focus-115x250.jpg 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 277px) 100vw, 277px\"></a></p>\n<p>Finally, Focus narrows the field range of hearing. When left off, hearing is from a full 360°. With Focus on, the field is narrowed to an area in front of the listener. This can help accentuate the voice of people you are talking with while lowering the distracting vocals behind and to the side.</p>\n<p>Earlier, I mentioned ANC, which is new to the IQbuds earphones. Their previous models relied on passive noise reduction only. Active noise canceling is interesting because some earphones and headphones do it better than others. Nuheara’s ANC is effective at knocking out most of the “droning” hum of background noise, such as an air conditioner, fan, or car noise. I prefer Apple’s ANC in their AirPods Pro earphones, but they don’t do all that the IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones do.<span class=\"Apple-converted-space\"> </span></p>\n<p>Note that while World On helps with hearing, it has no effect on how music sounds. Only ANC works with music apps.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_9.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304340\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_9.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"546\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_9.jpg 546w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_9-228x250.jpg 228w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 546px) 100vw, 546px\"></a></p>\n<p>Be careful with the volume setting, especially with ANC off. If the earphones are too loud, some high-pitched feedback can be heard. This has been an issue since the first IQbuds, but it is noticeably better with the IQbuds<sup>2</sup></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_1.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304348\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"424\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_1.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_1-300x212.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></a></p>\n<p>Even though the IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones are made to enhance hearing, they make a decent pair of earphones for music listening. The large 9.2 mm diameter dynamic speaker sounds fairly balanced between frequencies. Bassheads may be disappointed, but since these earphones’ purpose is hearing, the added accuracy of music reproduction is welcome. I could listen to music all day with these, from a comfort standpoint and musical quality—if the batteries lasted all day, that is.</p>\n<h2><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_6.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304343\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_6.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"458\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_6.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_6-300x229.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></a></h2>\n<h2>What I like</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Comfortable</li>\n<li>Great audio customization via App</li>\n<li>Effective ANC</li>\n<li>Clarifies vocals</li>\n<li>Filters out background noise</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>What I’d change</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Expensive</li>\n<li>Audio feedback sometimes happens</li>\n<li>Battery life isn’t as good as previous (and less expensive) IQbud Boost</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_2.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304347\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"483\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_2.jpg 483w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Nuheara_IQbud_Max_2-201x250.jpg 201w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 483px) 100vw, 483px\"></a></h2>\n<h2>Final Thoughts</h2>\n<p>The Nuheara IQbuds<sup>2</sup> Max earphones are an improvement over the original IQbuds and also the iQbuds Boost earphones—especially in comfort. While battery life may be limited when compared to other earphones, the improvement in hearing and clarity coupled with musical accuracy makes them worth considering for those of us with auditory issues.</p>\n<p><b>Price: </b>$399 US<span class=\"Apple-converted-space\"><br>\n</span><b>Where to buy: </b><a href=\"https://www.nuheara.com\" target=\"_blank\">Nuheara</a><br>\n<b>Source:</b> The sample of this product was provided by <a href=\"https://www.nuheara.com\" target=\"_blank\">Nuheara</a>.</p>\n  <p>Filed in categories: <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/category/reviews/\"
