600px\"></p>\n<p><strong>REVIEW</strong> – What’s something on your bucket list that you can tackle without traveling? What’s that? You said you’d learn to play guitar, bass or ukulele? Well, Fender’s Play app can help you cross that one off in whatever time increments you can devote. Fender was gracious enough to not only give us access to the app, but also loan us a guitar to use while we put the app through its paces. Let’s take a closer look at both.</p>\n<h2>What is it?</h2>\n<p>Fender Play is an online course that will teach you the basics of guitar, bass or ukulele. The step-by-step lessons are led by knowledgeable instructors assisted by clear videos, visuals and tablature resulting in clear information you can absorb on your own schedule without any judgement.</p>\n<h2>What’s in the App…</h2>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304037\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"630\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02.png 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02-300x189.png 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02-800x504.png 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02-768x484.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Download the Fender Play app (you can find it in Apple App Store or on Google Play)</li>\n<li>Free trial (cancel anytime)</li>\n<li>Special offer – Get 10% off guitars, amps and gear</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>And in the loaner box?</h2>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304038\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02a.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"351\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02a.jpg 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02a-300x105.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02a-800x281.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-02a-768x270.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<ul>\n<li>A Fender Player Mustang guitar</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Hardware specs (guitar)</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>24” scale length; “C”-shaped maple neck</li>\n<li>Two Mustang single-coil pickups</li>\n<li>9.5”-radius maple fingerboard with 22 medium jumbo frets</li>\n<li>Six-saddle string-through-body hardtail Strat® bridge with bent steel saddles</li>\n<li>Master Volume and Tone controls; three-way pickup switch</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Design and features (app)</h2>\n<p>The app is laid out with different paths for you to follow.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304028\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-03.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"473\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-03.jpg 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-03-300x142.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-03-800x378.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-03-768x363.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<p>You can choose from…</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Acoustic or Electric Guitar with focuses on Rock, Blues, Folk, Country or Pop</li>\n<li>Bass Guitar with focuses on Funk or Rock</li>\n<li>Ukulele</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Inside your path there are 5 levels for you to progress through, each with up to 21 courses. Each course has a number of lessons and/or practice modes with videos, charts and/or tablature to follow. Here are screens from Level 1 and Course 1 for Bass.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304031\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-06.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"713\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-06.jpg 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-06-300x214.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-06-800x570.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-06-768x548.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<p>Level 1 / Course 1 for guitar starts off with basics on how to hold and tune your guitar along with string basics.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304029\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-04.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"698\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-04.jpg 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-04-300x209.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-04-800x558.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-04-768x536.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<p>All along the way you are taught by talented musicians that speak clearly and provide all the information needed for the lesson at hand. You are free to pause and rewind and absorb at your own pace as you progress towards becoming a player.</p>\n<h3>Setup (app)</h3>\n<p>All you need to do is download the App and dive in. We loaded it up on my iPad Pro and my daughter’s iPhone SE. If you’d rather learn in front of your computer, you can also <a href=\"https://connect.fender.com/sign-up?ref=https://www.fender.com/play/plans?\" target=\"_blank\">log into</a> the service from a browser.</p>\n<p>From there you’ll need to choose which instrument you want to learn or “A Path” in the app. We chose electric guitar to go with the beautiful Player series Mustang guitar that Fender loaned us.</p>\n<p>If you don’t have an instrument yet, the initial lesson for a path will walk you through an instrument type calling out the different parts, functions and vocabulary. You’ll obviously need a guitar, bass or ukulele to actually start playing, but your new knowledge should prove helpful in discovering what you might be looking for. Not all of us have that one friend with too many guitars, so check with your local shop as many may allow rental dollars to go towards an eventual purchase.</p>\n<h3>Performance (app)</h3>\n<p>The thing about learning guitar always used to be finding a good teacher (friend, dad or instructor) and then working music you actually like into the lessons. If either of those weren’t quite right it made lessons tedious, frustrating or both.</p>\n<p>The Fender Play app solves the good teacher part of that equation from the get go. Within the guitar path, instructors rotate out from course to course for some variety, with all of them being easy to understand and as patient as I need them to be (I have a pause button after all).</p>\n<p>The below shot shows how clearly they show finger positions for chords. Compared to how I originally learned from just a paper chord chart, it’s really nice to have a clear image of proper finger and hand positioning. I realize that I sound old in the age of YouTube where one can find instruction on anything under the sun, but everything is here in a single, curated place with a progression order that is thought through and content that is age appropriate for everyone.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304034\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-09.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1432\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-09.jpg 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-09-175x250.jpg 175w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-09-559x800.jpg 559w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-09-768x1100.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<p>On the music side the simplified versions of songs within the Rock path were great fits for me and ones I would pick from a list if given the option. There are typically 4-5 five songs per level, but here are some stand outs.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Level 1 includes great songs like <em>Satisfaction</em> by the Rolling Stones and <em>Come As You Are</em> by Nirvana.</li>\n<li>Level 2 has Judas Priest’s <em>Breaking the Law </em>and <em>Bad Moon Rising</em> by Creedence Clearwater Revival among others.</li>\n<li>Level 3 serves up a few like the classic <em>Louie Louie</em> by The Kingsmen and Weezer’s <em>Buddy Holly.</em>\n</li>\n<li>Level 4 rocks with <em>Carry on Wayward Son</em> by Kansas and <em>White Wedding</em> by Billy Idol.</li>\n<li>And Level 5 finishes strong with ZZ Top’s <em>La Grange</em> and <em>Purple Haze</em> by none other than Jimi Hendrix.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>You’ll start with tuning and single note melodies with visuals and tablature before learning simplified chords and chord charts. As you move along, the difficulty ramps up as you’re ready to take on more. You’re able to repeat lessons and sections as much as you want. Your progress is kept by the app should you switch devices or even take a few days off, letting you start back in right where you left off.</p>\n<p>If you’ve dug into any of my previous music device reviews you may be aware that my son has been playing jazz guitar for nearly 1o years while I’m more of a three-chord punk type guy. My daughter Talula learned some chords and a couple of songs from Satch but has not had any other instruction, so she volunteered to dive in and give Fender Play (and the Mustang) a good run through.</p>\n<p>My own sessions with Fender Play were fun. While the first intro courses covered all the stuff I already know, I appreciated the content and the pace with which it was delivered. I learned the string names from knowing music theory as a vocalist, but the high-to-low string mnemonic the app used… <strong>E</strong>aster <strong>B</strong>unnies <strong>G</strong>et <strong>D</strong>izzy <strong>A</strong>t <strong>E</strong>aster definitely had me laughing.</p>\n<p>You’re able to change the playback speed in the practice sessions which is super useful if full pace is too fast at first. As a new player it takes some time to start developing muscle memory and finger dexterity.</p>\n<p>You can change paths for either instrument or genre at any point by clicking the<em> “Instrument: Genre Path” </em>header in the top left. After selecting a different instrument and/or a new genre’s “<em>Make this my path”</em> you have to click “<em>Done</em>” in the upper right to make your way back to courses.</p>\n<p>Here’s what the tablature looks like for <em>Hit Me With Your Best Shot</em> by Pat Benatar (Level 4), as you practice along.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/oTViyWAR9Co\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n<p>And here’s Talula playing what she learned. Fun part is that she said this isn’t a song she would have picked herself, but she digs it and is glad she learned it.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/CCQ6DNksPx0\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n<p>I also asked Satch to take a quick look at the App. He spent about an hour with it and gave me a “<em>this is pretty Good!</em>” nod, commenting that the Rock path difficulty was pretty mellow, but Level 5 on the Blues path felt a good deal more complicated in the higher levels.</p>\n<p>The app also isn’t just course progression. On the bottom nav bar, there’s a ton of <strong><em>Songs</em></strong> to dig into, a <strong><em>Skills</em></strong> section for continuing to learn, <strong>Collections </strong>for almost any interest (Crash Course: Punk Rock!) and a <em><strong>More…</strong></em><em> </em>section where you can manage your account, set practice reminders and more.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304032\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-07.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"353\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-07.jpg 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-07-300x106.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-07-800x282.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-07-768x271.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<h3>How about that guitar?</h3>\n<p>If any of you were wondering about the loaner guitar, this section’s for you. Here’s some pics of this beauty. It’s a Player series Mustang in a Gold Mist metallic color made from Alder with really comfortable curves and radii. The body has a bit more of a traditional shape than <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/2018/08/09/fender-player-series-jaguar-guitar-review/\">Jaguar we reviewed</a> almost two years ago.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304035\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-10.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"889\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-10.jpg 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-10-281x250.jpg 281w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-10-800x711.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-10-768x683.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<p>The headstock is the same sporting chrome tuners and a string tee for the High E and A strings.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304036\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-11.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1118\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-11.jpg 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-11-224x250.jpg 224w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-11-716x800.jpg 716w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-11-768x859.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<p>The neck is Maple with jumbo frets, a 24″ scale and a comfortable 9.5″ radius on the fingerboard. Both the bridge and neck pickups are Mustang single coils with a 3-position switch for selection duties.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304033\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-08.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1230\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-08.jpg 1000w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-08-203x250.jpg 203w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-08-650x800.jpg 650w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/FPLY-08-768x945.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\"></p>\n<p>The hardtail, string-through-body body bridge keeps things locked down and increases sustain. Normally I would have removed the sticker and pick guard protective layer, but left them on since this is a loaner after all.</p>\n<h2>What I like</h2>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>APP</strong></li>\n<li>Free trial and bonus 10% discount on instruments, amps and gear</li>\n<li>Evenly paced lessons that cover the basics and get you playing</li>\n<li>Great selection of genres, bands and songs</li>\n<li><strong>Guitar</strong></li>\n<li>Easy to tune and play, good neck shape</li>\n<li>Affordable and great for beginners to hacks like myself</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>What I’d change</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>(App) I’d separate the instrument from music genre path as you’re more likely to jump between genres</li>\n<li>Not much else</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Final thoughts</h2>\n<p>The Fender Play App is a great resource for players of any level. It’s definitely aimed at newcomers but there’s plenty to dig into for someone like myself that just learned what I learned and didn’t get all the foundation. With a free trial period, it’s really easy to jump in and give it a shot. Now which one of your friends has a guitar you can borrow?</p>\n<p><strong>Price</strong>: $9.99 per month (app) | $599.99 Player Series Mustang® guitar<br>\n<strong>Where to buy</strong>: <a 13:50:41","updatedTime":"2020-08-31 13:50:41","title":"Wotancraft PILOT Camera Messenger Bag review","link":"https://the-gadgeteer.com/?p=303750","description":"\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304584\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-22-e1597839898542.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"460\" height=\"460\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-22-e1597839898542.jpg 460w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-22-e1597839898542-250x250.jpg 250w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 460px) 100vw, 460px\"></p>\n<p><strong>REVIEW</strong> – Vintage style combined with superb functionality. That’s what Wotancraft is all about, and I’m seeing plenty of both in the Pilot Camera Messenger Bag. This little guy is a solid multitasker that will appeal to both photographer and the daily carry crowd without compromises. It looks good, too! We’ve got a lot of pictures in this one. To the review!</p>\n<h2>What is it?</h2>\n<p>It’s a messenger bag and a camera bag that adds modular expandability to meet your specific needs.</p>\n<h2>What’s in the box?</h2>\n<p>I’m reviewing the 10 Liter version of the bag. The bag includes 3 dividers for camera equipment (2 with lids), a detachable shoulder strap &#38; shoulder pad, and a storage bag.</p>\n<p>My review package also included 4 add-on modules available with the purchase. We’ll walk through them in the review.</p>\n<h2>Hardware specs</h2>\n<p>This bag comes in two sizes. I’m testing the Medium size which specs out as follows:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Overall dimensions: 40 x 16 x 28 cm.</li>\n<li>Cordura 500D tear-proof waxed canvas</li>\n<li>Water-repellant teflon exterior coating, PU laminated interior coating</li>\n<li>10 liter capacity</li>\n<li>Total weight 900 grams</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Design and features</h2>\n<p>Hailing from Taipei City, Taiwan, Wotoncraft’s design aesthetic is inspired by vintage military styles &#38; materials. The Lightweight Camera and Messenger bag I’m testing clearly pulls influences from WWII Swiss Army ammunition bags. Check out that sweet front profile.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304563\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"441\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-1.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-1-300x221.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>The material is a lightweight Cordura 500D waxed canvas that weighs in at a <span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">paultry 900 grams overall. But don’t be deceived by the light weight; this build is serious business. Ultra </span>strength<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> nylon threading, YKK zips, zinc alloy &#38; brass hardware, Duraflex buckles and snap hooks… all the components are built for heavy use.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">While the style is vintage, you’ll find that the </span>Wotancraft<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> Lightweight Messenger is packed with contemporary design and some really clever innovations. Let’s start on the outside and work our way in.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">The backside includes a luggage pass-through and a 32 cm by 20.5 cm zipper pocket for papers and such that uses a sealed YKK zipper (with a zipper garage) to keep the wet from getting to your precious papers and notebooks.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304564\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"448\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-2.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-2-300x224.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">A simple grab handle sits is smallish, but that’s OK given the overall size of the bag. It won’t get in your way when you don’t need it.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304567\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-5.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"548\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-5.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-5-274x250.jpg 274w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">A pair of straps on the base of the bag allow you to tether a </span>tripod<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> or umbrella. These straps can be removed and attached to the loops on the front face of the bag if you prefer.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304568\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-6.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"440\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-6.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-6-300x220.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>Those loops run the height of the front face of the bag, providing attachment points for carabiners and other accessories.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304624\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-31.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"495\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-31.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-31-300x248.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">Dual side pockets will stash water bottles, </span>sunglass<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> cases, and similar items. I love the way the pockets swing around and attach to the inside of the front panel. It’s a little thing, but this allows you to stash extra-fat items in these pockets like a chunky hydration bottle. </span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304571\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-9-575x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"575\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-9-575x800.jpg 575w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-9-180x250.jpg 180w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-9.jpg 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 575px) 100vw, 575px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">And that front panel hides another trick. Behind the panel is a pass-through that holds a mesh pocket to hide valuables. The really cool part of this secret pocket is that is accessible with vertical zips on both sides of the bag for added flexibility.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304570\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-8.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"674\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-8.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-8-223x250.jpg 223w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">Let’s talk about that flap to the main compartment. It locks in place with a hook that is adjustable so that you cinch the bag down for smaller loadouts. </span><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">Now check out those wings of fabric when I open the flap. See those </span>triangular<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> bits </span>at the<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> top of the bag? They keep stuff from falling out of the bag (or being grabbed by wandering hands), despite there being only one latch point keeping it anchored. They also keep the wet out of the interior of the bag when you’re on the go. </span><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">Super clever.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304588\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-26.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"704\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-26.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-26-213x250.jpg 213w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">You’ll find a front pocket on the bag that has two smaller pockets inside, perfect for your small stuff like phones. I have a pocketknife and earbuds in here. The sub-pockets are identically sized for easy organizing.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304569\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-7.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"401\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-7.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-7-300x201.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">Now on to the main compartment. This space is configurable with multiple dividers that are included with your purchase. You’ll find a padded laptop divider and three camera divider inserts (two with lids) as shown below. </span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304573\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-11.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"421\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-11.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-11-300x211.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">This gives you all sorts of options to configure the main compartment to your needs. Here’s the </span>interior<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> cleared of all the dividers.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304590\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-28.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"450\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-28.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-28-300x225.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">Here’s the laptop divider inserted. It will take a 13″ </span>MacBook<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> or 12.9″ iPad.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304589\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-27.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"450\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-27.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-27-300x225.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304572\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-10.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-10.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-10-188x250.jpg 188w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">And here’s one example of the space with the laptop divider removed </span>and the<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> camera divider inserts in place. You can reconfigure the compartments as needed based on the gear you’re carrying at the time.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304591\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-29.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"450\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-29.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-29-300x225.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">The build uses a “surgical grade microfiber” designed to resist pulling from adding and removing the velcro bits. This stuff is STRONG. Adding and removing dividers can be a wrestling match in that smaller space, but nothing is moving once you lock the pieces in place</span><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">Your carry strap is also made of tough stuff. I love these beefy Duraflex swivel buckles. </span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304566\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-4.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"644\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-4.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-4-233x250.jpg 233w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px;\">There’s plenty of length in the shoulder strap to find a comfy fit. A generous </span>shoulder<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"> pad with neoprene SCUBA fabric is a nice bonus for comfort.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304565\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-3.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"345\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-3.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-3-300x173.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<h3>Accessories</h3>\n<p>Wotancraft makes a series of add-on accessories for the Lightweight Messenger Camera Bag to add organization above and beyond what’s included in the bag. I got four different accessories to play with.</p>\n<p>The first two accessories are made to velcro to the panels on the interior main pocket. The Zipperless Pocket Module is a pocket with a hood, made for quick access. I have my mouse in this module, but it’s plenty big for a phone or additional components. I also like this one for collecting random small bits (like loose change or small tools).</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304574\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-12.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"771\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-12.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-12-195x250.jpg 195w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>The second velcro accessory is the Cord Organizer/Utility Fastener Module. It basically three wide elastic bands that will hold your MacBook power brick, batteries, cables, and other stuff you don’t want floating around in your bag. They make a version of this specifically for extra camera batteries and SD cards if that’s your thing.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304580\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-18-577x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"577\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-18-577x800.jpg 577w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-18-180x250.jpg 180w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-18.jpg 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 577px) 100vw, 577px\"></p>\n<p>Either module will velcro to any of the interior panels of the main compartment. Here I have one attached to the laptop divider and the other to the front wall of the bag, but you can find all sorts of combinations with the camera divider inserts too.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304582\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-20.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"682\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-20.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-20-220x250.jpg 220w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304581\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-19.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"656\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-19.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-19-229x250.jpg 229w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>The next two add-ons are external pockets. These use YKK snap-on clips to attach to the loops on the front face of the bag. The Zipper Pouch includes an external webbed pocket and three more wide elastic loops for bits like your headphones.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304577\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-15.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"797\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-15.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-15-188x250.jpg 188w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304578\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-16.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"736\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-16.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-16-204x250.jpg 204w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>The Drawstring Pouch will handle a 500 ml water bottle.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304575\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-13.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"772\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-13.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-13-194x250.jpg 194w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>Flip either of these modular pockets over, and you’ll find those clips.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304576\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-14.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"728\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-14.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-14-206x250.jpg 206w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>They pop easily onto the loops on the bag exterior.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304579\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-17.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"694\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-17.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-17-216x250.jpg 216w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>And BOOM! You’re accessorized.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304584\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-22.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\"></p>\n<p>As an added bonus, these two modules come with carry straps so that you detach them from the bag and sling them over your shoulder for a hike or a walk through town.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304587\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-25.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-25.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-25-250x250.jpg 250w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<h3>Performance</h3>\n<p>The Wotancraft Lightweight Messenger and Camera Bag packs excellent usability into a surprisingly small and lightweight package. It’s easy to maneuver, and perfect for straight-up messenger use if you’re rocking a laptop and your office stuff. Here’s a shot of the bag without the accessory pockets.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304586\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-24.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-24.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-24-250x250.jpg 250w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>And here’s another with the optional Zipper Pouch and Drawstring Pouch attached.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304583\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-21.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-21.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-21-250x250.jpg 250w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>No matter how you configure the bag, you’re getting excellent usability. Small bags can be problematic when it comes to accessibility as you add pockets and features that cramp the space of the main compartment. This is especially important if you don’t want to be fiddling around in your main compartment for quick-grab items like keys, phones, headphones, etc.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304585\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-23.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-23.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-23-250x250.jpg 250w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p>The Wotancraft Pilot Camera Messenger also shines with respect to flexibility. You can reconfigure this bag for travel, for the daily office commute, for photo sessions, or for simple daytrips with a few tweaks to your add-ons and inserts. It’s a great multitasker, and that lightweight build makes it extremely shoulder friendly for long days.</p>\n<p>I’m also impressed with the overall carrying capacity. While it is only listed at 10 liters overall, the external pocketing and onboard modules on this bag are designed in such a way that they don’t compromise the main space. I find myself being able to load this thing up with as much stuff as I get in some of my 15- or 20-liter bags that have more rigid geometry.</p>\n<h2>What I like</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Super lightweight.</li>\n<li>Excellent organization and overall usability.</li>\n<li>Flexible and adaptable, especially when you leverage the add-on modules.</li>\n<li>Many configurations in one bag without compromising any details.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>What needs to be improved</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>The velcro used on the inserts is super strong. This is great for stability, but can make for some wrestling to get the inserts into (or out of) position.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Final thoughts</h2>\n<p>This is my first experience with the Wotoncraft brand, and I’m really impressed. Excellent usability, simple functionality, modular flexibility, and vintage styling make this bag a true multitasker that fits a number of use cases. I’d wouldn’t just recommend this bag for photographers. There’s a lot to love for daily use and folks that carry a lot of tech gear as well. I’m looking forward to seeing more from this brand!</p>\n<p><strong>Price</strong>: $199. Accessory pricing varies, but discounts are included if you bundle them with purchase of your bag.<br>\n<strong>Where to buy</strong>: Follow this link to the <a target=\"_blank\">product page on the Wotancraft web site</a>.<br>\n<strong>Source</strong>: The sample of this product was provided by <a href=\"https://www.wotancraft.tw/en\" target=\"_blank\">Wotancraft</a>.</p>\n  <p>Filed in categories: <a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/category/reviews/\" rel=\"category tag\">Reviews</a></p><p>Tagged: <a -414_1d09274fd249399f.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-28.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn21@2020_6/2020/08/31/05-50-48-033_a80db0113474ed6b.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-27.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn92@2020_1/2020/08/31/05-50-46-806_9c1970942b86e210.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-10.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn96@2020_5/2020/08/31/05-51-00-150_2103c4223e735e15.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-29.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn76@2020_6/2020/08/31/05-50-54-747_ea476ae7f5b64f51.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn87@2020_4/2020/08/31/05-50-46-227_8db01116e1cd547d.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-3.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn26@2020_6/2020/08/31/05-51-00-241_844d17e79023539d.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn82@2020_3/2020/08/31/05-50-57-472_dcc131f391701a43.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-18-577x800.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn45@2020_5/2020/08/31/05-50-47-798_7fd36e3ccb7331c4.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-20.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn90@2020_3/2020/08/31/05-50-57-716_d5d2ed37486241f2.webp","https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Wotancraft-PilotCameraMessengerBag-19.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn72@2020_3/2020/08/31/05-50-46-931_53bbe6cc4 OrCreatedDate":1598853041839},{"createdTime":"2020-08-31 13:50:41","updatedTime":"2020-08-31 13:50:41","title":"Rock Space Whole House Mesh Wifi System review","link":"https://the-gadgeteer.com/?p=303494","description":"\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-1-2.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-303518\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-1-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"516\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-1-2.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-1-2-300x194.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-1-2-768x495.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></a></p>\n<p><strong>REVIEW</strong> – Over the years I have tried some of those wifi repeater products to boost the wifi signal in the dead spots in our house.  I was never really satisfied with the spotty results, and many of them require that you give it an SSID that is different than your main SSID.  And sometimes my devices would connect to the repeater even though the wifi strength was better connecting to another repeater in the house.  Anyway, I have never been really happy with those things, so I finally decided to give one of these ‘mesh wifi’ products a shot now that prices have seemingly come down as more competition is in the market.  I tested the Rock Space Whole Home Mesh Wifi product to see if those pesky dead spots disappeared.</p>\n<h2><strong>What is it?</strong></h2>\n<p>Three small boxes that you place around your house that communicate with each other, creating a ‘mesh’ wifi network.  The main box is located where your internet connection comes in the house, then it boosts the wifi signal to the other 2 boxes so that your wifi signal is stronger all over the house instead of just having 1 wifi router where the internet comes in the house.  All 3 boxes also use the same SSID (name of your wireless network) and password, making it easy to simply connect to 1 wireless network.</p>\n<h2><strong>What’s in the box?</strong></h2>\n<ul>\n<li>3 Rock Space mesh units, with power supplies</li>\n<li>1 gigabit Ethernet cable</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><strong>Here are the wireless specs:</strong></h2>\n<ul>\n<li>IEEE 802.11 ac/n/a/ 5 GHz, IEEE 802.11 b/g/n 2.4 GHz</li>\n<li>Signal rate: 867 Mbps at 5 GHZ, 300 Mbps at 2.4 GHz</li>\n<li>Security: WPA/WPA2-PSK</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><strong>Here are the hardware specs:</strong></h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Ports: 2 LAN/WAN gigabit Ethernet ports, DC-in 2.1mm</li>\n<li>Power: 12V/1A</li>\n<li>Size: 4 in x 4 in x 4 in</li>\n<li>Weight: each unit weighs 10 oz.</li>\n<li>Model:  AC1200</li>\n</ul>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-3.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-303496\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-3.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"543\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-3.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-3-300x204.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-3-768x521.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Features and performance</strong></h2>\n<p>Each mesh box is about 4 inches square, colored black, and the top has a grey fabric surface on it.  On the bottom of the box are mounting holes to attach it to a wall if you wanted.  On the bottom are also the connections for the power cable and 2 Ethernet ports, 1 for connecting to your existing internet connection coming into your house, or the other for connecting to the Ethernet ports you may have in the walls of your house.  On top of each unit is a small LED light that gives you a status of the connection. I think it fits in with the décor in the house pretty easily and the size makes it pretty easy to place them where you need them.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-2.jpg\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-303497\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"501\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-2.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-2-300x188.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Rock-Space-wifi-mesh-2-768x481.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></a></p>\n<p>Setup was pretty easy.  Just follow the included instructions, which include downloading the free app. (I am on Android, and it worked great!)  I plugged up the Rock Space where the internet comes into my house (in the back of the house right next to the bedroom and office).  I have a 2-story shotgun-type of house that is twice as deep as it is wide.  So with the internet router at the back of the house, it is almost impossible to get a good signal on the front porch, as well as on the second floor at the front of the house.  So I picked the living room on the main floor at the front of the house for the second Rock Space unit (right next to our wifi-enabled Samsung TV), and the 3<sup>rd</sup> unit I placed upstairs in the bonus room at the front of the house.  We have almost given up trying to get a signal in those places, so I was eager to see if the Rock Space could solve that.</p>\n<p>Before I mention my test results, let me comment on the various features available with the Rock Space, which are many.  First of all, the security features are very strong.  Protecting your wireless network from hackers becomes more important every day, so having the WPA2-TSK protocol is the minimum that I would expect.  In layman’s terms, what WPA2-TSK does is create a unique encrypted connection password (called a ‘key’) between the Rock Space boxes and every device on the network, and that special encrypted key is automatically, constantly changed so it is not easy to break.  The technology provides a much higher level of security than just plain WPA, which hackers can break in minutes.  It is true that higher levels of wireless security are rolling out, and WPA2-TSK is not impossible to break, but for now, everyone needs to be using WPA2-TSK at the very minimum.</p>\n<p>The Rock Space also includes a firewall that provides some great features, which you set inside the app.  For example, you can block specific websites you don’t want available on your network.  You can create a temporary ‘guest’ wireless network and password that times out after a set amount of time.  You can create groups and add devices to those groups (for example “kid’s devices”) and then add as many devices as you want to those groups.  Then you can disable access to all of them with 1 click.  Pretty cool.  If you are going to have more than 30 devices connected at once to your network (like during a party) you can turn on ‘capacity-oriented mode’ to control the bandwidth to all the devices.  The Rock Space has UPnP, which means it automatically recognizes the required ports of gaming devices, P2P devices, etc.</p>\n<p>The Rock Space also has a feature called QoS (Quality of service), which means that you can specify what the maximum upload and download speed should be for every device on the network and no device will be able to go over those speeds.  In this way, devices such as a gaming consoles or streaming movie services can’t hog the entire bandwidth.  This is particularly helpful for those folks who work out of their home and don’t want the kid’s hogging the bandwidth!  You cannot, however, get granular control over which devices are limited in bandwidth, which would be really nice. The limits you set apply to every device.  Some other products with QoS features do provide the ability to have granular control over specific devices, but the Rock Space QoS feature is a simple version and doesn’t provide that.</p>\n<p>The Rock Space also uses the MU-MIMO technology, which is awesome.  Again, in laymen’s terms, that means that when multiple devices are using bandwidth they all share the bandwidth.  Basically, that means that all devices on the network download at the same speed instead of fighting to get the same speed.  It just makes things smoother and with less buffering.</p>\n<h2><strong>Now, a word about how I tested the Rock Space</strong></h2>\n<p>What I did first was leave my existing wireless network in place and plug the first Rock Space device into the back of my existing router using the Ethernet cable. Then I set up the other 2 Rock Space mesh devices around the house.  That way, I had 2 wireless networks that I could test at the same time.  So I then went around to locations in the house and tested the upload/download speeds of my existing router (I did 10 tests at each location and averaged the results).  I then did the same thing with the Rock Space SSID.  So I had 2 sets of results that I could use to compare the 2 different wireless networks.  And yes, before you ask, when I tested the Rock Space network I disabled the SSID on the existing router so that network wouldn’t disrupt my up/down speeds!</p>\n<p>What I discovered was that the Rock Space mesh network performed just as good as the router from my internet provider and eliminated the dead spots on the front porch and the upstairs bonus room at the front of the house because I placed the 2<sup>nd</sup> and 3<sup>rd</sup> mesh devices close to the front of the house.  It was wonderful. No more dead spots! The Rock Space also has a feature called ‘fast roaming’ that will automatically switch your device to the nearest mesh device if you are moving around the house.  I tested this and it worked great with my cellphone.  The app even has several screens where you can see which devices are connected to each mesh device, and you can even look at how much bandwidth (up and down) that any individual device is pulling at that moment.  So you can easily troubleshoot which device in your house might be hogging bandwidth at any moment.  Pretty neat.</p>\n<p>Finally, the app also lets you check for firmware updates and automatically install them on each mesh device.  Nice touch.</p>\n<h2>What I like</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Great price</li>\n<li>Easy-to-use setup and a great smart-phone app</li>\n<li>Strong security</li>\n<li>Many firewall features</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>What I’d change</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Not much.  I would like more granular control over individual device bandwidth usage</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><strong>Final thoughts</strong></h2>\n<p>I am now a fan of mesh networks.  The convenience of having control over the network through an easy-to-use app is great, and the automatic “fast roaming” switching for my devices was seamless.  Setup was easy and worked with the instructions provided.  The security features provide me with some level of comfort, and the dead spots have been eliminated in my house, which is probably the best part of the whole thing. I compared the price of the Rock Space to other mesh network products and the price is very competitive.  There are mesh networking devices out there that have the very latest wireless networking protocols with much higher speeds, but right now they are much more expensive, and my internet connection couldn’t take advantage of those speeds anyway.  My negatives are basically none, and really the only feature I would want to see enhanced is more control over specific devices in the QoS section of the app.  But at $129.99 on Amazon, I see no reason not to purchase this.  If you have dead spots in your house and want more control over your network, with a strong level of security to protect yourself, the Rock Space is a great product!</p>\n<p><strong>Price</strong>: $149.99<br>\n<strong>Where to buy</strong>: Buy here on <a href=\"https://amzn.to/3aZRhbc\" rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\">Amazon</a> and <a loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304299\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_10.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"610\" height=\"800\" 100vw, 610px\"></strong></p>\n<p><strong>REVIEW</strong> – It is forecasted to be hotter and drier than normal through fall across the lower 48. This means that residents should water conservatively. The Scotts Gro 7 is a smart sprinkler controller that can precisely control the watering schedule and use local weather to water intelligently. Read on to see what I think!</p>\n<h2>What is it?</h2>\n<p>The Scotts Gro 7 Zone controller is a device that connects to the solenoids that determine what zone is watered in an underground sprinkler system. The system also connects to a local 2.4 GHz Wi-Fi network. The Scotts Gro is controlled through the cloud with an app that runs on iOS or Android, or through a smart speaker powered by Alexa or Google Home. The controller was at one time branded as the Blossom. I actually have the Blossom controller but it works with the new app and as a like-for-like equivalent product.</p>\n<h2>What’s in the box?</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Controller</li>\n<li>Power Supply</li>\n<li>Wall Screws</li>\n<li>Wire Labels</li>\n<li>Quick Start Guide</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Hardware specs</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Zones: 7 (8 if not using a pump start relay)</li>\n<li>Connectivity: Wi-Fi</li>\n<li>Placement: Indoors</li>\n<li>EPA WaterSense Certified: Yes</li>\n<li>Dimensions: 6.95″ x 6.95″ x 1.55″</li>\n<li>Power input: 120 VAC</li>\n<li>Station input: 24 VAC</li>\n<li>Zone detection: automatic</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Design and features</h2>\n<p>The Scotts Gro 7 Zone controller is different than most every other controller on the market. While most of the other controllers have faceplates of confusing buttons and switches, electromechanical timers, or hard to read and cryptic LCDs, like my old controller below, the Gro has a single glowing LED in its center. It looks like the environmentally friendly cousin of HAL 9000, without the penchant for eavesdropping or insubordination.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-304294\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_05.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_05.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_05-188x250.jpg 188w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></p>\n<p> </p>\n<p>The design of the chassis takes into consideration that the unit must be wired by the user but also ensures that the integrated circuit board is protected. the front cover is easily removed to reveal the terminal block for wiring the stations but also keeps the main circuitry hidden behind a translucent plastic panel.</p>\n<p>The terminal block uses spring-loaded fasteners to hold the station wiring in place, so no bending wires around screws is required.</p>\n<p>The unit is powered by a 120 power adapter attached to a 6 foot cable. Normally, an irrigation controller is installed at least 6 feet from an outlet or power source, so this should meet most installation requirements.</p>\n<h3>Setup</h3>\n<p>Setup does involve a handful of steps but they are all easy and well documented in the literature that comes with the unit. The instructions are written out in English and include detailed pictures or diagrams so that no guesswork is required that is normally expected for assembling furniture.</p>\n<p><strong><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304291\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_02-800x267.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"267\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_02-800x267.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_02-300x100.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_02-768x256.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_02-1536x512.jpg 1536w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_02-2048x683.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304292\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_03-800x263.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"263\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_03-800x263.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_03-300x99.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_03-768x252.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_03-1536x504.jpg 1536w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_03-2048x673.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304293\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_04-800x263.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"263\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_04-800x263.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_04-300x99.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_04-768x252.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_04-1536x505.jpg 1536w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_04-2048x673.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></strong></p>\n<p>The steps include:</p>\n<p>1. Label the wires on the existing system so that each zone is numbered consistently on the old and new system and that the common wire is identified. The system comes with self adhesive labels with pre-printed numbers.</p>\n<p><strong><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304295\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_06-800x373.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"373\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_06-800x373.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_06-300x140.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_06-768x358.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_06-1536x716.jpg 1536w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_06.jpg 1717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></strong></p>\n<p>2. Remove the old controller. Before doing this it may help to record the existing settings if the current watering scheme is providing satisfactory results. The old weather sensors may also be removed. The new controller uses real-time weather forecasts from the internet to adjust watering.</p>\n<p><strong><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304297\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_08.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_08.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_08-188x250.jpg 188w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></strong></p>\n<p>3. Install the new controller. The screws provided mount through the front panel.</p>\n<p><strong><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304298\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_09.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_09.jpg 600w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_09-188x250.jpg 188w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\"></strong></p>\n<p>4. Connect the wires to the corresponding ports on the new controller. The controller supports a pump start relay used in irrigation systems that draw upon a well for a water source. This may also be attached to the main solenoid if the irrigation system comes of an artesian well. If neither of these situations applies to the irrigation system then this circuit may be used to control the 8th zone.</p>\n<p>5. Power the controller</p>\n<p>6. Record the pairing code off of the front of the unit and attach the faceplate.</p>\n<p><strong><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-304296\" src=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_07-800x600.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"600\" srcset=\"https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_07-800x600.jpg 800w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_07-300x225.jpg 300w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_07-768x576.jpg 768w, https://the-gadgeteer.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Scotts_Gro_07.jpg 1067w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\"></strong></p>\n<p>7. Download the app. The GRO app will work with the Blossom controller. The reverse may not be true. Setting up the app and account will allow control and monitoring of the irrigation system from anywhere there is internet access.</p>\n<p>8. Pair the controller to the existing Wi-Fi. The Blossom requires a 2.4GHz network.</p>\n<p>9. Pair the controller to the app account. This requires using the code that is on the inner faceplate of the controller.</p>\n<h3>Operation</h3>\n<p>Operating the Gro from the mobile app is easier than using a traditional zone controller, mostly because it does not require the operator to be directly near wherever the controller is installed. For each zone there are a number of different options that can be set. The watering schedule allows for Fixed days of the week, interval days of 2 through 7 days, or odd or even days. The watering time can be set for sunrise, sunset, or a specified time. The sunrise and sunset times allow hourly offsets from two hours before up to two hours after each event.</p>\n<p>The watering mode allows for either smart watering or a custom duration. A custom duration allows just a specific time to water. Smart watering adjusts watering based on the plant type: succulents, shrubs, flowers, trees or grass (in order of how much water each type of plant needs). The watering mode also bases the time on the nozzle type: drip, bubbler, sprays, rotors and sprinklers. There is a switch to indicate if the area gets rainfall. Finally, there is a slider to adjust rainfall from 20% t 210% of the calculated values the program selects.</p>\n<p>On the zone screen there is also an option to set a soak cycle so that the watering will happen multiple times a day. This is useful to limit runoff of water.</p>\n<p>There is an on-demand portion of the app that allows running a particular zome or running all of the zones for a specified time.</p>\n<p>Lastly, there is a section that shows a historical calendar of what zone was run and for how long.</p>\n<p>While the app is very useful, there are some things I wish the app were better at. When there is a program running the app does not provide notifications that it is operating or that a cycle has started. The app does alert the operator that a cycle will be skipped based on the sufficient amount of recent rainfall. Also, there is no ability to pause the operation, so that someone may cross the yard to put away a toy, for example. These are two things that a mobile controlled irrigation system should be designed to do.</p>\n<p>When your phone is not around you can turn the irrigation system on or off using an Alexa or Google Home smart speaker. The smart speaker will turn all zones on, turn on a specified zone for a specified time, or stop all watering.</p>\n<h3>Performance</h3>\n<p>Some existing product reviews have correctly indicated that if the internet is disconnected that the device will not function. This is an accurate assessment – it does not seem that the device is preloaded with cycle information and even if it were, that controlling the pre-programmed cycle would be impossible.</p>\n<h2>What I like</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Very configurable and easy to read app</li>\n<li>lots of control options</li>\n<li>Easy Set up</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>What I’d change</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Allow the watering to be paused</li>\n<li>put a play / pause button on the controller</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Final thoughts</h2>\n<p>The added flexibility and local weather control the Scotts Gro has mare than makes up for the lack of a local on off button. For more money there are competitors from Orbit and Rachio that have more zones and a local display.</p>\n<p><strong>Price</strong>: $65.90<br>\n<strong>Where to buy</strong>: <a href=\"https://amzn.to/3aZZlZD\" rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\">Amazon</a><br>\n<strong>Source</strong>: This product was purchased with my own funds.</p>\n  <p>Filed in categories: <a
